[exact](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#exact "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") thisAll goals completed! 🐙 ```
Lean also has a `let` tactic, which is similar to the `have` tactic, but is used to introduce local definitions instead of auxiliary facts. It is the tactic analogue of a `let` in a proof term:
`example : ∃ x, x + 2 = 8 := by⊢ [∃](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Quantifiers/#Exists___intro "Documentation for Exists in Lean Language Reference") x[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Quantifiers/#Exists___intro "Documentation for Exists in Lean Language Reference") x [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 2 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 8   [let](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#let "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") a : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") := 3 * 2a:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") := 3 [*](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference") 2⊢ [∃](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Quantifiers/#Exists___intro "Documentation for Exists in Lean Language Reference") x[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Quantifiers/#Exists___intro "Documentation for Exists in Lean Language Reference") x [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 2 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 8   [exists](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#exists "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") aAll goals completed! 🐙 ```
As with `have`, you can leave the type implicit by writing `let a := 3 * 2`. The difference between `let` and `have` is that `let` introduces a local definition in the context, so that the definition of the local declaration can be unfolded in the proof.
We have used `.` to create nested tactic blocks. In a nested block, Lean focuses on the first goal, and generates an error if it has not been fully solved at the end of the block. This can be helpful in indicating the separate proofs of multiple subgoals introduced by a tactic. The notation `.` is whitespace sensitive and relies on the indentation to detect whether the tactic block ends. Alternatively, you can define tactic blocks using curly braces and semicolons:
`example (p q r : Prop) : p ∧ (q ∨ r) ↔ (p ∧ q) ∨ (p ∧ r) := byp:Propq:Propr:Prop⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation [show](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#show "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") p ∧ (q ∨ r)mpr.inlp:Propq:Propr:Proph✝:p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference");       [rename_i](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#rename_i "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") hpqmpr.inlp:Propq:Propr:Prophpq:p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference");       [exact](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#exact "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ⟨hpq.[left](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And.left in Lean Language Reference"), [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference") hpq.[right](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And.right in Lean Language Reference")⟩All goals completed! 🐙 }     {mpr.inrp:Propq:Propr:Proph✝:p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") [show](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#show "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") p ∧ (q ∨ r)mpr.inrp:Propq:Propr:Proph✝:p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference");       [rename_i](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#rename_i "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") hprmpr.inrp:Propq:Propr:Prophpr:p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference");       [exact](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#exact "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ⟨hpr.[left](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And.left in Lean Language Reference"), [Or.inr](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inr in Lean Language Reference") hpr.[right](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And.right in Lean Language Reference")⟩All goals completed! 🐙 } } ```
It is useful to use indentation to structure proof: every time a tactic leaves more than one subgoal, we separate the remaining subgoals by enclosing them in blocks and indenting. Thus if the application of theorem `foo` to a single goal produces four subgoals, one would expect the proof to look like this:

```
  apply foo
  . <proof of first goal>
  . <proof of second goal>
  . <proof of third goal>
  . <proof of final goal>

```

or

```
  apply foo
  case <tag of first goal>  => <proof of first goal>
  case <tag of second goal> => <proof of second goal>
  case <tag of third goal>  => <proof of third goal>
  case <tag of final goal>  => <proof of final goal>

```

or

```
  apply foo
  { <proof of first goal>  }
  { <proof of second goal> }
  { <proof of third goal>  }
  { <proof of final goal>  }

```

##  5.5. Tactic Combinators[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=tactic-combinators "Permalink")
_Tactic combinators_ are operations that form new tactics from old ones. A sequencing combinator is already implicit in the `by` block:
`example (p q : Prop) (hp : p) : p ∨ q :=   byp:Propq:Prophp:p⊢ p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") q [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference")hp:Propq:Prophp:p⊢ p; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
Here, `[apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference"); [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` is functionally equivalent to a single tactic which first applies `[apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference")` and then applies `[assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")`.
In `t₁ ``<;>`` t₂`, the `<;>` operator provides a _parallel_ version of the sequencing operation: `t₁` is applied to the current goal, and then `t₂` is applied to _all_ the resulting subgoals:
`example (p q : Prop) (hp : p) (hq : q) : p ∧ q :=   byp:Propq:Prophp:phq:q⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")leftp:Propq:Prophp:phq:q⊢ prightp:Propq:Prophp:phq:q⊢ q <;>leftp:Propq:Prophp:phq:q⊢ prightp:Propq:Prophp:phq:q⊢ q [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
This is especially useful when the resulting goals can be finished off in a uniform way, or, at least, when it is possible to make progress on all of them uniformly.
The `first`` | t₁ | t₂ | ... | tₙ` applies each `tᵢ` until one succeeds, or else fails:
`example (p q : Prop) (hp : p) : p ∨ q := byp:Propq:Prophp:p⊢ p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") q   [first](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#first "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference")hp:Propq:Prophp:p⊢ p; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") Or.inr; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")  ``example (p q : Prop) (hq : q) : p ∨ q := byp:Propq:Prophq:q⊢ p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") q   [first](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#first "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference")hp:Propq:Prophq:q⊢ p; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")hp:Propq:Prophq:q⊢ p | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inr](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inr in Lean Language Reference")hp:Propq:Prophq:q⊢ q; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
In the first example, the left branch succeeds, whereas in the second one, it is the right one that succeeds. In the next three examples, the same compound tactic succeeds in each case:
`example (p q r : Prop) (hp : p) : p ∨ q ∨ r := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:p⊢ p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r   [repeat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#repeat "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ([first](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#first "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference")hp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:p⊢ p; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") Or.inr | [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (p q r : Prop) (hq : q) : p ∨ q ∨ r := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophq:q⊢ p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r   [repeat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#repeat "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ([first](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#first "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference")h.hp:Propq:Propr:Prophq:q⊢ q; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inr](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inr in Lean Language Reference")hp:Propq:Propr:Prophq:q⊢ q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r | [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (p q r : Prop) (hr : r) : p ∨ q ∨ r := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophr:r⊢ p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r   [repeat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#repeat "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ([first](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#first "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inl in Lean Language Reference")h.hp:Propq:Propr:Prophr:r⊢ r; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")h.hp:Propq:Propr:Prophr:r⊢ q | [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Or.inr](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or.inr in Lean Language Reference")h.hp:Propq:Propr:Prophr:r⊢ r | [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙) ```
The tactic tries to solve the left disjunct immediately by assumption; if that fails, it tries to focus on the right disjunct; and if that doesn't work, it invokes the assumption tactic.
You will have no doubt noticed by now that tactics can fail. Indeed, it is the “failure” state that causes the _first_ combinator to backtrack and try the next tactic. The `[try](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#try "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` combinator builds a tactic that always succeeds, though possibly in a trivial way: `try`` t` executes `t` and reports success, even if `t` fails. It is equivalent to `first``| t |``skip`, where `skip` is a tactic that does nothing (and succeeds in doing so). In the next example, the second `[constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` succeeds on the right conjunct `q ∧ r` (remember that disjunction and conjunction associate to the right) but fails on the first. The `[try](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#try "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic ensures that the sequential composition succeeds:
`example (p q r : Prop) (hp : p) (hq : q) (hr : r) : p ∧ q ∧ r := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r   [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ prightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r <;>leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ prightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r ([try](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#try "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")right.leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ qright.rightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ r) <;>leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ pright.leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ qright.rightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ r [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
Be careful: `repeat`` (``try`` t)` will loop forever, because the inner tactic never fails.
In a proof, there are often multiple goals outstanding. Parallel sequencing is one way to arrange it so that a single tactic is applied to multiple goals, but there are other ways to do this. For example, `all_goals`` t` applies `t` to all open goals:
`example (p q r : Prop) (hp : p) (hq : q) (hr : r) : p ∧ q ∧ r := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r   [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ prightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r   [all_goals](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#all_goals "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ([try](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#try "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")right.leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ qright.rightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ r)   [all_goals](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#all_goals "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
In this case, the `any_goals` tactic provides a more robust solution. It is similar to `all_goals`, except it succeeds if its argument succeeds on at least one goal:
`example (p q r : Prop) (hp : p) (hq : q) (hr : r) : p ∧ q ∧ r := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r   [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ prightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r   [any_goals](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#any_goals "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")right.leftp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ qright.rightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ r   [any_goals](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#any_goals "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
The first tactic in the `by` block below repeatedly splits conjunctions:
`example (p q r : Prop) (hp : p) (hq : q) (hr : r) :       p ∧ ((p ∧ q) ∧ r) ∧ (q ∧ r ∧ p) := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference")[(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference")p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") p   [repeat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#repeat "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ([any_goals](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#any_goals "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")right.right.right.rightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ p)   [all_goals](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#all_goals "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
In fact, we can compress the full tactic down to one line:
`example (p q r : Prop) (hp : p) (hq : q) (hr : r) :       p ∧ ((p ∧ q) ∧ r) ∧ (q ∧ r ∧ p) := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference")[(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference")p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") r [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") p   [repeat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#repeat "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ([any_goals](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#any_goals "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") ([first](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#first "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") | [constructor](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#constructor "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")right.right.right.rightp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:qhr:r⊢ p | [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙)) ```
The combinator `focus`` t` ensures that `t` only effects the current goal, temporarily hiding the others from the scope. So, if `t` ordinarily only effects the current goal, `focus`` (``all_goals`` t)` has the same effect as `t`.
##  5.6. Rewriting[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=rewriting "Permalink")
The `rw` tactic and the `simp` tactic were introduced briefly in [Calculational Proofs](Quantifiers-and-Equality/#calculational-proofs). In this section and the next, we discuss them in greater detail.
The `rw` tactic provides a basic mechanism for applying substitutions to goals and hypotheses, providing a convenient and efficient way of working with equality. The most basic form of the tactic is `rw`` [t]`, where `t` is a term whose type asserts an equality. For example, `t` can be a hypothesis `h : x = y` in the context; it can be a general lemma, like `[add_comm](Inductive-Types/#add_comm "Definition of example") : ∀ x y, x + y = y + x`, in which the rewrite tactic tries to find suitable instantiations of `x` and `y`; or it can be any compound term asserting a concrete or general equation. In the following example, we use this basic form to rewrite the goal using a hypothesis.
`[variable](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___variable "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") (k : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (f : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (h₁ : f 0 = 0) (h₂ : k = 0) : f k = 0 := byk:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")f:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h₁:f 0 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0h₂:k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0⊢ f k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [h₂]k:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")f:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h₁:f 0 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0h₂:k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0⊢ f 0 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0 -- replace k with 0   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [h₁]All goals completed! 🐙 -- replace f 0 with 0 ```
In the example above, the first use of `[rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` replaces `k` with `0` in the goal `f k = 0`. Then, the second one replaces `f 0` with `0`. The tactic automatically closes any goal of the form `t = t`. Here is an example of rewriting using a compound expression:
`example (x y : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (p : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Prop) (q : Prop) (h : q → x = y)         (h' : p y) (hq : q) : p x := byx:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")y:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")p:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Propq:Proph:q → x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") yh':p yhq:q⊢ p x   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [h hq]x:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")y:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")p:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Propq:Proph:q → x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") yh':p yhq:q⊢ p y; [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
Here, `h hq` establishes the equation `x = y`.
Multiple rewrites can be combined using the notation `rw`` [t_1, ..., t_n]`, which is just shorthand for `rw``[t_1]; ...;``rw`` [t_n]`. The previous example can be written as follows:
`[variable](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___variable "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") (k : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (f : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (h₁ : f 0 = 0) (h₂ : k = 0) : f k = 0 := byk:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")f:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h₁:f 0 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0h₂:k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0⊢ f k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [h₂, h₁]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
By default, `[rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` uses an equation in the forward direction, matching the left-hand side with an expression, and replacing it with the right-hand side. The notation `←t` can be used to instruct the tactic to use the equality `t` in the reverse direction.
`[variable](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___variable "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") (a b : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (f : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (h₁ : a = b) (h₂ : f a = 0) : f b = 0 := bya:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")b:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")f:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h₁:a [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") bh₂:f a [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0⊢ f b [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [←h₁, h₂]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
In this example, the term `←h₁` instructs the rewriter to replace `b` with `a`. In the editors, you can type the backwards arrow as `\l`. You can also use the ASCII equivalent, `<-`.
Sometimes the left-hand side of an identity can match more than one subterm in the pattern, in which case the `rw` tactic chooses the first match it finds when traversing the term. If that is not the one you want, you can use additional arguments to specify the appropriate subterm.
`example (a b c : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : a + b + c = a + c + b := bya:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")b:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")c:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")⊢ a [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") b [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") c [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") a [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") c [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") b   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Nat.add_assoc, Nat.add_comm b, ← Nat.add_assoc]All goals completed! 🐙  ``example (a b c : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : a + b + c = a + c + b := bya:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")b:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")c:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")⊢ a [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") b [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") c [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") a [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") c [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") b   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Nat.add_assoc, Nat.add_assoc, Nat.add_comm b]All goals completed! 🐙  ``example (a b c : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : a + b + c = a + c + b := bya:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")b:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")c:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")⊢ a [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") b [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") c [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") a [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") c [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") b   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Nat.add_assoc, Nat.add_assoc, Nat.add_comm _ b]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
In the first example above, the first step rewrites `a + b + c` to `a`` + (``b + c``)`. The next step applies commutativity to the term `b + c`; without specifying the argument, the tactic would instead rewrite `a`` + (``b + c``)` to `(``b + c``) + ``a`. Finally, the last step applies associativity in the reverse direction, rewriting `a`` + (``c`` + ``b``)` to `a + c + b`. The next two examples instead apply associativity to move the parenthesis to the right on both sides, and then switch `b` and `c`. Notice that the last example specifies that the rewrite should take place on the right-hand side by specifying the second argument to `Nat.add_comm`.
By default, the `[rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic affects only the goal. The notation `rw`` [t] ``at`` h` applies the rewrite
`example (f : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (a : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (h : a + 0 = 0) : f a = f 0 := byf:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")a:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h:a [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 0 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0⊢ f a [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") f 0   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Nat.add_zero] at hf:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")a:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h:a [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0⊢ f a [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") f 0   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [h]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
The first step, `[rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [Nat.add_zero] at h`, rewrites the hypothesis `a + 0 = 0` to `a [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0`. Then the new hypothesis `a [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0` is used to rewrite the goal to `f 0`` = ``f 0`.
The `[rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic is not restricted to propositions. In the following example, we use `rw`` [h] ``at`` t` to rewrite the hypothesis `t : Tuple α n` to `t : Tuple α`` 0`.
`def Tuple (α : Type) (n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) :=   { as : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α // as.[length](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___length "Documentation for List.length in Lean Language Reference") = n }  ``example (n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (h : n = 0) (t : Tuple α n) : Tuple α 0 := byα:Typen:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h:n [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0t:Tuple α n⊢ Tuple α 0   [rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [h] at tα:Typen:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h:n [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0t:Tuple α 0⊢ Tuple α 0   [exact](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#exact "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") tAll goals completed! 🐙 ```
##  5.7. Using the Simplifier[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=using-the-simplifier "Permalink")
Whereas `rw` is designed as a surgical tool for manipulating a goal, the simplifier offers a more powerful form of automation. A number of identities in Lean's library have been tagged with the `[simp]` attribute, and the `simp` tactic uses them to iteratively rewrite subterms in an expression.
`example (x y z : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : (x + 0) * (0 + y * 1 + z * 0) = x * y := byx:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")y:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")z:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")⊢ [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference")x [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 0[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") [*](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference")0 [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") y [*](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference") 1 [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") z [*](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference") 0[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") x [*](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference") y   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙  ``example (x y z : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (p : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Prop) (h : p (x * y))         : p ((x + 0) * (0 + y * 1 + z * 0)) := byx:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference")x [*](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference") y[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference")⊢ p [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference")[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference")   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")x:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")y:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")p:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Proph:p [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference")x [*](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference") y[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference")⊢ p [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference")x [*](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference") y[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference"); [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
In the first example, the left-hand side of the equality in the goal is simplified using the usual identities involving 0 and 1, reducing the goal to `x * y`` = ``x * y`. At that point, `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` applies reflexivity to finish it off. In the second example, `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` reduces the goal to `p (x * y)`, at which point the assumption `h` finishes it off. Here are some more examples with lists:
`[open](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___open "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") List  ``example (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") [reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") (xs ++ [1, 2, 3]) = [3, 2, 1] ++ [reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") xs := As with `[rw](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rw "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")`, you can use the keyword `at` to simplify a hypothesis:
`example (x y z : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (p : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Prop)         (h : p ((x + 0) * (0 + y * 1 + z * 0))) : p (x * y) := byx:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")y:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")z:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")p:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Proph:p [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HMul___mk "Documentation for HMul.hMul in Lean Language Reference")[(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference")x [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 0[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") Moreover, you can use a “wildcard” asterisk to simplify all the hypotheses and the goal:

For operations that are commutative and associative, like multiplication on the natural numbers, the simplifier uses these two facts to rewrite an expression, as well as _left commutativity_. In the case of multiplication the latter is expressed as follows: `x * (y * z) = y * (x * z)`. The `local` modifier tells the simplifier to use these rules in the current file (or section or namespace, as the case may be). It may seem that commutativity and left-commutativity are problematic, in that repeated application of either causes looping. But the simplifier detects identities that permute their arguments, and uses a technique known as _ordered rewriting_. This means that the system maintains an internal ordering of terms, and only applies the identity if doing so decreases the order. With the three identities mentioned above, this has the effect that all the parentheses in an expression are associated to the right, and the expressions are ordered in a canonical (though somewhat arbitrary) way. Two expressions that are equivalent up to associativity and commutativity are then rewritten to the same canonical form.
`[attribute](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Attributes/#Lean___Parser___Command___attribute "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") [local simp] Nat.mul_comm Nat.mul_assoc Nat.mul_left_comm [attribute](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Attributes/#Lean___Parser___Command___attribute "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") [local simp] Nat.add_assoc Nat.add_comm Nat.add_left_comm `

As with `rw`, you can send `simp` a list of facts to use, including general lemmas, local hypotheses, definitions to unfold, and compound expressions. The `simp` tactic also recognizes the `←t` syntax that `rewrite` does. In any case, the additional rules are added to the collection of identities that are used to simplify a term.
`def f (m n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") :=   m + n + m  ``example {m n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} (h : n = 1) (h' : 0 = m) : (f m n) = n := bym:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")n:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h:n [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 1h':0 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") m⊢ f m n [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") n   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [h, ←h', f]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
A common idiom is to simplify a goal using local hypotheses:
`[variable](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___variable "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") (k : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (f : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (h₁ : f 0 = 0) (h₂ : k = 0) : f k = 0 := byk:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")f:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h₁:f 0 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0h₂:k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0⊢ f k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [h₁, h₂]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
To use all the hypotheses present in the local context when simplifying, we can use the wildcard symbol, `*`:
`[variable](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___variable "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") (k : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (f : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (h₁ : f 0 = 0) (h₂ : k = 0) : f k = 0 := byk:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")f:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")h₁:f 0 [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0h₂:k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0⊢ f k [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [*]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
Here is another example:

[+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") y [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") u   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [*, Nat.add_comm]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
The simplifier will also do propositional rewriting. For example, using the hypothesis `p`, it rewrites `p ∧ q` to `q` and `p ∨ q` to `[True](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Truth/#True___intro "Documentation for True in Lean Language Reference")`, which it then proves trivially. Iterating such rewrites produces nontrivial propositional reasoning.
`example (p q : Prop) (hp : p) : p ∧ q ↔ q := byp:Propq:Prophp:p⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") q [↔](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Iff___intro "Documentation for Iff in Lean Language Reference") q   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [*]All goals completed! 🐙  ``example (p q : Prop) (hp : p) : p ∨ q := byp:Propq:Prophp:p⊢ p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") q   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [*]All goals completed! 🐙  ``example (p q r : Prop) (hp : p) (hq : q) : p ∧ (q ∨ r) := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:phq:q⊢ p [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [*]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
The next example simplifies all the hypotheses, and then uses them to prove the goal.
`set_option linter.unusedVariables false `
`example (u w x x' y y' z : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (p : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Prop)         (h₁ : x + 0 = x') (h₂ : y + 0 = y')         : x + y + 0 = x' + y' := byu:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 0 [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 0 One thing that makes the simplifier especially useful is that its capabilities can grow as a library develops. For example, suppose we define a list operation that symmetrizes its input by appending its reversal:
`def mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α) :=   xs ++ xs.[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") ```
Then for any list `xs`, `(mk_symm xs).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference")` is equal to `mk_symm xs`, which can easily be proved by unfolding the definition:
`def mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α) :=  xs ++ xs.[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") `
`theorem reverse_mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α)         : (mk_symm xs).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") = mk_symm xs := byα:Type u_1xs:[List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α⊢ (mk_symm xs).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") mk_symm xs   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [mk_symm]All goals completed! 🐙 ```
We can now use this theorem to prove new results:
`def mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α) :=  xs ++ xs.[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") theorem reverse_mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α)        : (mk_symm xs).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") = mk_symm xs := byα:Type u_1xs:[List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α⊢ (mk_symm xs).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") mk_symm xs  [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [mk_symm]All goals completed! 🐙 `
