But using `reverse_mk_symm` is generally the right thing to do, and it would be nice if users did not have to invoke it explicitly. You can achieve that by marking it as a simplification rule when the theorem is defined:
`def mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α) :=  xs ++ xs.[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") `
`@[simp] theorem reverse_mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α)         : (mk_symm xs).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") = mk_symm xs := byα:Type u_1xs:[List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α⊢ (mk_symm xs).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") mk_symm xs   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [mk_symm]All goals completed! 🐙  ``example (xs ys : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference"))         : (xs ++ mk_symm ys).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") = mk_symm ys ++ xs.[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") := byxs:[List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")ys:[List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") ys[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAppend___mk "Documentation for HAppend.hAppend in Lean Language [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙  ``example (xs ys : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") The notation `@[simp]` declares `reverse_mk_symm` to have the `[simp]` attribute, and can be spelled out more explicitly:
`def mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α) :=  xs ++ xs.[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") `

The attribute can also be applied any time after the theorem is declared:

Once the attribute is applied, however, there is no way to permanently remove it; it persists in any file that imports the one where the attribute is assigned. As we will discuss further in [Attributes](Interacting-with-Lean/#attributes), one can limit the scope of an attribute to the current file or section using the `local` modifier:
`def mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α) :=  xs ++ xs.[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") `

Outside the section, the simplifier will no longer use `reverse_mk_symm` by default.
Note that the various `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` options we have discussed—giving an explicit list of rules, and using `at` to specify the location—can be combined, but the order they are listed is rigid. You can see the correct order in an editor by placing the cursor on the `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` identifier to see the documentation string that is associated with it.
There are two additional modifiers that are useful. By default, `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` includes all theorems that have been marked with the attribute `[simp]`. Writing `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") only` excludes these defaults, allowing you to use a more explicitly crafted list of rules. In the examples below, the minus sign and `only` are used to block the application of `reverse_mk_symm`.
`def mk_symm (xs : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α) :=   xs ++ ys).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference"))         : p ((mk_symm ys).[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") ++ The `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic has many configuration options. For example, we can enable contextual simplifications as follows:
`example : [if](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") x = 0 [then](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") y + x = y [else](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") x ≠ 0 := byx:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")y:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")⊢ if x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0 then y [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") y else x ≠ 0   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") +[contextual](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/The-Simplifier/Configuring-Simplification/#Lean___Meta___Simp___Config___mk "Documentation for Lean.Meta.Simp.Config.contextual in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
With `+[contextual](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/The-Simplifier/Configuring-Simplification/#Lean___Meta___Simp___Config___mk "Documentation for Lean.Meta.Simp.Config.contextual in Lean Language Reference")`, the `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic uses the fact that `x = 0` when simplifying `y + x = y`, and `x ≠ 0` when simplifying the other branch. Here is another example:
`example : ∀ (x : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (`unused variable `h`  Note: This linter can be disabled with `set_option linter.unusedVariables false``h : x = 0), y + x = y := byy:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")⊢ ∀ (x : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")), x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 0 → y [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") y [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") +[contextual](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/The-Simplifier/Configuring-Simplification/#Lean___Meta___Simp___Config___mk "Documentation for Lean.Meta.Simp.Config.contextual in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
Another useful configuration option is `+[arith](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/The-Simplifier/Configuring-Simplification/#Lean___Meta___Simp___Config___mk "Documentation for Lean.Meta.Simp.Config.arith in Lean Language Reference")` which enables arithmetical simplifications.
`example : 0 < 1 + x ∧ x + y + 2 ≥ y + 1 := byx:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")y:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")⊢ 0 [<](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt in Lean Language Reference") 1 [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") x [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") x [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") y [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 2 ≥ y [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 1   [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") +[arith](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/The-Simplifier/Configuring-Simplification/#Lean___Meta___Simp___Config___mk "Documentation for Lean.Meta.Simp.Config.arith in Lean Language Reference")All goals completed! 🐙 ```
##  5.8. Split Tactic[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=split-tactic "Permalink")
The `[split](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#split "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic is useful for breaking nested `if`-`then`-`else` and `match` expressions in cases. For a `match` expression with `nnn` cases, the `[split](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#split "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic generates at most `nnn` subgoals. Here is an example:
`def f (x y z : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") :=   [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") x, y, z [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   | 5, _, _ => y   | _, 5, _ => y   | _, _, 5 => y   | _, _, _ => 1  ``example (x y z : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : x ≠ 5 → y ≠ 5 → z ≠ 5 → z = w → f x y w = 1 := byw:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")x:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")y:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")z:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")⊢ x ≠ 5 → y ≠ 5 → z ≠ 5 → z [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") w → f x y w [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") 1   [intros](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#intros "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language [f]w:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")z:[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")a✝³:x ≠ 5a✝²:y ≠ 5a✝¹:z ≠ 5a✝:z [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") w⊢ (match x, y, w with   | 5, x, x_1 => y   | x, 5, x_1 => y   | x, x_1, 5 => y   | x, x_1, x_2 => 1) [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language We can compress the tactic proof above as follows.
`def f (x y z : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") :=  [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") x, y, z [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")  | 5, _, _ => y  | _, 5, _ => y  | _, _, 5 => y  | _, _, _ => 1 `

The tactic `[split](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#split "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") <;> [first](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#first "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") | [contradiction](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#contradiction "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") | [rfl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` first applies the `[split](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#split "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic, and then for each generated goal it tries `[contradiction](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#contradiction "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")`, and then `[rfl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` if `[contradiction](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#contradiction "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` fails. Like `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")`, we can apply `[split](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#split "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` to a particular hypothesis:
`def g (xs ys : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") :=   [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") xs, ys [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   | [a, b], _ => a+b+1   | _, [b, _] => b+1   | _, _      => 1  ``example (xs ys : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") ##  5.9. Extensible Tactics[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=extensible-tactics "Permalink")
In the following example, we define the notation `triv` using the command `[syntax](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Notations-and-Macros/Defining-New-Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Command___syntax "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")`. Then, we use the command `[macro_rules](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Notations-and-Macros/Macros/#Lean___Parser___Command___macro_rules "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")` to specify what should be done when `triv` is used. You can provide different expansions, and the tactic interpreter will try all of them until one succeeds:
`-- Define a new tactic notation [syntax](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Notations-and-Macros/Defining-New-Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Command___syntax "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") "triv" : tactic  ``[macro_rules](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Notations-and-Macros/Macros/#Lean___Parser___Command___macro_rules "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   | `(tactic| triv) => `(tactic| [assumption](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (h : p) : p := byp:Sort ?u.2129h:p⊢ p   trivAll goals completed! 🐙  ``-- You cannot prove the following theorem using `triv` -- example (x : α) : x = x := by --  triv  -- Let's extend `triv`. The tactic interpreter -- tries all possible macro extensions for `triv` until one succeeds [macro_rules](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Notations-and-Macros/Macros/#Lean___Parser___Command___macro_rules "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   | `(tactic| triv) => `(tactic| [rfl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference"))  ``example (x : α) : x = x := byα:Sort u_1x:α⊢ x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") x   trivAll goals completed! 🐙  ``example (x : α) (h : p) : x = x ∧ p := byα:Sort u_1p:Propx:αh:p⊢ x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") x [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") p   [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [And.intro](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And.intro in Lean Language Reference")leftα:Sort u_1p:Propx:αh:p⊢ x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") xrightα:Sort u_1p:Propx:αh:p⊢ p <;>leftα:Sort u_1p:Propx:αh:p⊢ x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") xrightα:Sort u_1p:Propx:αh:p⊢ p trivAll goals completed! 🐙  ``-- We now add a (recursive) extension [macro_rules](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Notations-and-Macros/Macros/#Lean___Parser___Command___macro_rules "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") | `(tactic| triv) => `(tactic| [apply](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") And.intro <;> triv)  ``example (x : α) (h : p) : x = x ∧ p := byα:Sort u_1p:Propx:αh:p⊢ x [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") x [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") p   trivAll goals completed! 🐙 ```
##  5.10. Exercises
  1. Go back to the exercises in [Propositions and Proofs](Propositions-and-Proofs/#propositions-and-proofs) and [Quantifiers and Equality](Quantifiers-and-Equality/#quantifiers-and-equality) and redo as many as you can now with tactic proofs, using also `rw` and `simp` as appropriate.
  2. Use tactic combinators to obtain a one-line proof of the following:


``declaration uses 'sorry'`example (p q r : Prop) (hp : p) : (p ∨ q ∨ r) ∧ (q ∨ p ∨ r) ∧ (q ∨ r ∨ p) := byp:Propq:Propr:Prophp:p⊢ [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")q [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") p [∨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") r[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference") [∧](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#And___intro "Documentation for And in Lean Language Reference") [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Or___inl "Documentation for Or in Lean Language Reference")q
